We want to formilise in HoTT the intuition behind a correspondance between the
concept of *PathOver* and its respective *total space*. The term PathOver was
briefly mentioned in {% cite hottbook %} and later defined in {% cite Licata2015
%}. It is extensivily used in {%cite hott-in:agda %}.

![](/assets/png-images/2018-07-05-geometry-intution-of-pathovers-7f9fb342.png)

Let's review first an equility type that is closely relted with these pathovers.
(See also {% cite Licata2015 %} for some extra comments).

{: .foldable}

## Homogeneous equality

> `Path {A} a₀ a₁` is sometimes called **homogeneous equality**, because it
> relates two elements a₀ and a₁ whose types are *definitionally/judgementally
> equal*.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="1026" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="1032" class="Number">30</a> <a id="1035" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1045" class="Datatype Operator">_==_</a>

## Heterogeneous equality

> In {%cite McBride2004 %} the author introduced a *heterogeneous equality*, which is an equality type
> `a:A= b:B` that relates two elements `a:A` and `b:B` which may have two judgementally
> distinct types, though the reflexivity constructor applies only when both the
> two types and the two terms are judgementally equal.

> However, McBride’s heterogeneous equality is **logically equivalent** to a
> homogeneous equality type *satisfying uniqueness of identity proofs*, which
> is undesirable **in homotopy type theory, because not all types should be sets**.

> This heterogeneous equality relates two elements of two different types along a
> specific equality α between the types

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="1864" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="HEq₁"></a><a id="1869" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1869" class="Datatype">HEq₁</a> <a   <a id="9267" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Homotopy"></a><a id="9274" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9274" class="Module">Homotopy</a> <a id="9283" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9284" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9284" class="Bound">ℓᵢ</a> <a id="9287" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9287" class="Bound">ℓⱼ</a><a id="9289" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9291" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9292" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9292" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9294" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9296" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="9301" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9284" class="Bound">ℓᵢ</a><a id="9303" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9305" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9306" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9306" class="Bound">P</a> <a id="9308" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9310" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9292" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9312" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9314" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="9319" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9287" class="Bound">ℓⱼ</a><a id="9321" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9323" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="9333" class="Comment">-- A homotopy is a natural isomorphism between two functions, we will write</a>
    <a id="9413" class="Comment">-- f ∼ g when (f x == g x) for all x.</a>
    <a id="hott.Homotopy.homotopy"></a><a id="9455" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9455" class="Function">homotopy</a> <a id="9464" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9466" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9467" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9467" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="9469" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9469" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="9471" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9473" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="9475" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9475" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9477" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9479" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9292" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9480" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9482" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9484" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9306" class="Bound">P</a> <a id="9486" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9475" class="Bound">x</a><a id="9487" class="Symbol">))</a> <a id="9490" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9492" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="9497" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9498" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9284" class="Bound">ℓᵢ</a> <a id="9501" href="Agda.Primitive.html#657" class="Primitive Operator">⊔</a> <a id="9503" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#9287" class="Bound">ℓⱼ</a><a id="9505" class="Symbol">)</a>

    <a id="13033" class="Comment">-- Application of an homotopy</a>

    <a id="13136" class="Comment">-- The axiom of function extensionality postulates that the</a>
    <a id="13200" class="Comment">-- application of homotopies is an equivalence.</a>

  <a id="15943" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Propositions"></a><a id="15950" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#15950" class="Module">Propositions</a> <a id="15963" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="15974" class="Comment">-- A type is a mere proposition if any two inhabitants of the type</a>
    <a id="16045" class="Comment">-- are equal</a>
    <a id="hott.Propositions.isProp"></a><a id="16062" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#16062" class="Function">isProp</a> <a id="16069" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="16071" class="Symbol">∀{</a><a id="16073" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#16073" class="Bound">ℓ</a><a id="16074" class="Symbol">}</a>  <a id="16077" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="16078" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#16078" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="16080" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="16082" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="16087" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#16073" class="Bound">ℓ</a><a id="16088" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="16090" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="16092" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="16097" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#16073" class="Bound">ℓ</a>

    <a id="23305" class="Comment">-- Half-adjointness implies equivalence.</a>
    <a id="hott.Halfadjoints.ishae-≃"></a><a id="23350" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#23350" class="Function">ishae-≃</a> <a id="23358" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="23360" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="23361" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#23361" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="23363" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="23365" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#20672" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="23367" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="23369" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#20686" class="Bound">B</a><a id="23370" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="23372" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="23374" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#20750" class="Record">ishae</a> <a id="23380" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#23361" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="23382" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="23384" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#20672" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="23386" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#11945" class="Function Operator">≃</a> <a id="23388" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#20686" class="Bound">B</a>

    <a id="26103" class="Comment">-- Quasiinverses create equivalences.</a>

       <a id="27733" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#2603" class="Field">fst</a> <a id="27737" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="27738" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#27329" class="Function">invEqv</a> <a id="27745" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#27657" class="Bound">α</a><a id="27746" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="27748" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#3014" class="Function Operator">∘</a> <a id="27750" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#2603" class="Field">fst</a> <a id="27754" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#27657" class="Bound">α</a>     <a id="27760" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#3777" class="Function Operator">==⟨</a> <a id="27764" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#13453" class="Function">funext</a> <a id="27771" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="27772" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#12751" class="Function">rlmap-inverse-h</a> <a id="27788" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#27657" class="Bound">α</a><a id="27789" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="27791" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#3777" class="Function Operator">⟩</a>

  <a id="27814" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="27819" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#26525" class="Module">EquivalenceComposition</a> <a id="27842" class="Keyword">public</a>

<a id="27850" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="27855" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#2466" class="Module">hott</a> <a id="27860" class="Keyword">public</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


Let be `α : A == B`, `a : A`, and `b : B` then the following types are equivalent
to `HEq`.

### Equivalences

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="28425" class="Comment">-- A proof that HEq₁-≃-HEq₂</a>

  <a id="28501" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28501" class="Function">HEq₁-to-HEq₂</a> <a id="28514" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28516" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="28517" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28517" class="Bound">α</a> <a id="28519" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28521" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28467" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="28523" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1045" class="Datatype Operator">==</a> <a id="28526" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28480" class="Bound">B</a><a id="28527" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="28529" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28529" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="28531" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28533" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28467" class="Bound">A</a><a id="28534" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="28536" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28536" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="28538" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28540" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#28480" class="Bound">B</a><a id="28541" class="Symbol">}</a>

Finally, we complete the chain of equivalence with `HEq₄-≃-HEq₁`.

{: .foldable}

For the follwing discussion, we may use heterogeneous using the first definition.

## Path over a path

The PathOver is the depedent version of a *path*, what it exactly means is that
we have a path between two endpoints from maybe different types but with. Which
is exactly the same definition of the heterogeneous equality. The difference is
that PathOvers simplifies the `HEq` definition by factorizing the type family
that is involved in the paths.

We first define `PathOver₁` as the inductive family with only one constructor,
the reflexivity over the reflexivity on the base space `A`. To eliminate this
type, we can use path-over induction. In Agda, we just do pattern matching on
the path in the base `A`. We can also define this notion of PathOvers in at least
other four different ways. Let's such definitions all equivalent.

- <pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="32813" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="PathOver₁"></a><a id="32818" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32818" class="Datatype">PathOver₁</a> <a id="32828" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="32829" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32829" class="Bound">ℓ</a><a id="32830" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="32832" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="32833" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32833" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="32835" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="32837" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="32841" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32829" class="Bound">ℓ</a><a id="32842" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="32844" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32845" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32845" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="32847" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="32849" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32833" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="32851" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="32853" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="32858" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32829" class="Bound">ℓ</a><a id="32859" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="32861" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="32862" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32862" class="Bound">a₁</a> <a id="32865" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="32867" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#32833" class="Bound">A</a><a id="32868" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="32870" class="Symbol">:</a>

<a id="33742" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33625" class="Function">PathOver₅</a> <a id="33752" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="33753" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="33755" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="33757" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33757" class="Bound">A</a><a id="33758" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="33760" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33760" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="33762" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1096" class="InductiveConstructor">idp</a> <a id="33766" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33766" class="Bound">c₁</a> <a id="33769" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33769" class="Bound">c₂</a> <a id="33772" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="33774" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33766" class="Bound">c₁</a> <a id="33777" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1045" class="Datatype Operator">==</a> <a id="33780" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33769" class="Bound">c₂</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Above when we used `transport C α c₁`, we could also have used `coe (ap C α)`,
both functions are of type `C a₁ → C a₂`. The other case with `c₂` is similar.

### Equivalences

{: .foldable}

      <a id="39845" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#39722" class="Function">PathOver₁~PathOver₅</a> <a id="39865" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1096" class="InductiveConstructor">idp</a> <a id="39869" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="39871" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#1096" class="InductiveConstructor">idp</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

We are going to use the fifth definition for pathovers, the one which is
using an inductive family.
<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="PathOver"></a><a id="40000" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40000" class="Function">PathOver</a> <a id="40009" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="40011" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#33625" class="Function">PathOver₅</a>

<a id="40022" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="40028" class="Number">30</a> <a id="40031" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40000" class="Function">PathOver</a>
<a id="40040" class="Keyword">syntax</a> <a id="40047" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40000" class="Function">PathOver</a> B p u v <a id="40064" class="Symbol">=</a> u == v [ B ↓ p ]{% endraw %}</pre>


> While we have motivated PathOver as a factored heterogeneous equality, there
> is also a geometric intuition. **Dependent types correspond to fibrations**, so a
> type `C : A → Type` can be pictured as its total space `∑ a:A . C` a projecting
> down to `A` by first projection.

> A **path-over** `γ : PathOver C α c­₁ c₂` represents a path σ in `∑ a:A . C` a
> a between `(a₁, c₁)` and `(a₂,c₂)`, such that ap fst σ is exactly `α`. That
> is, it is a path in the total space that projects down to, or lies over, `α`
> (path pairing `pair= α γ` will be made precise below)


## Total spaces

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="40703" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="40710" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40710" class="Module">_</a> <a id="40712" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="40713" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40713" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="40715" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40715" class="Bound">j</a><a id="40716" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="40718" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40718" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="40720" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="40722" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="40727" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40713" class="Bound">i</a><a id="40728" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="40730" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40730" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="40732" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="40734" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40718" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="40736" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="40738" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#761" class="Function">Type</a> <a id="40743" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40715" class="Bound">j</a><a id="40744" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="40746" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40746" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="40748" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40748" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="40750" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="40752" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40718" class="Bound">A</a><a id="40753" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="40755" class="Keyword">where</a>

      <a id="42019" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40764" class="Function">Σ-to-==[↓]</a>    <a id="42033" class="Comment">-- equivalence</a>
      <a id="42054" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="42056" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#40922" class="Function">==[↓]-to-Σ</a>  <a id="42068" class="Comment">-- inverse</a>
      <a id="42085" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#2583" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="42087" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="42088" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#41470" class="Function">Σ-to-==[↓]∘==[↓]-to-Σ∼id</a> <a id="42113" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#2583" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="42115" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-07-05-pathovers.md %}{% raw %}#41649" class="Function">==[↓]-to-Σ∘Σ-to-==[↓]∼id</a><a id="42139" class="Symbol">)))</a> <a id="42143" class="Comment">-- homotopies</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


## Other facts

We can build a dependent path by applying a depedent function to a homogeneous path.
